</div>
			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">College and university rankings</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
				</div>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p><b>College and university rankings</b> are <a href="/wiki/Rankings" class="mw-redirect" title="Rankings">rankings</a> of institutions in <a href="/wiki/Higher_education" title="Higher education">higher education</a> ordered by various combinations of various factors. Rankings have most often been conducted by magazines, newspapers, websites, governments, or academics. In addition to ranking entire institutions, organizations perform rankings of specific programs, departments, and schools. Various rankings consider combinations of measures of funding and endowment, research excellence and/or influence, specialization expertise, admissions, student options, award numbers, internationalization, graduate employment, industrial linkage, historical reputation and other criteria. Various rankings mostly evaluating on institutional output by <a href="/wiki/Research" title="Research">research</a>. Some rankings evaluate institutions within a single country, while others assess institutions worldwide. The subject has produced much debate about rankings' usefulness and accuracy.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> The expanding diversity in rating methodologies and accompanying criticisms of each indicate the lack of consensus in the field. Further, it seems possible to game the ranking systems through excessive self-citations.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> The variety of academic rankings provide a comprehensive overview and insightful overlook of different academic institutions on composite capabilities in <a href="/wiki/Academia" class="mw-redirect" title="Academia">academia</a>. Whilst <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> advocates for the beneficial role that <a href="/wiki/Higher_education" title="Higher education">higher education</a> could be the common good of social leverage and educating skills to equip everyone participated, yet college ranking is a transparent tool for a fair evaluation for the public.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_rankings">Global rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Global rankings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>See <a href="#Regional_and_national_rankings">Regional and national rankings</a> for university rankings within a particular region. Several organizations produce worldwide university rankings, including the following.</p>
<p>The three longest established and most influential global rankings are those produced by ShanghaiRanking Consultancy (the Academic Ranking of World Universities; ARWU), <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education" title="Times Higher Education">Times Higher Education</a> (THE) and <a href="/wiki/Quacquarelli_Symonds" title="Quacquarelli Symonds">Quacquarelli Symonds</a> (QS). All of these, along with other global rankings, primarily measure the research performance of universities rather than their teaching.<sup id="cite_ref-IHE_2010_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IHE_2010-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HEPI_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HEPI-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IHE_2016_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IHE_2016-8">[8]</a></sup> They have been criticised for being "largely based on what can be measured rather than what is necessarily relevant and important to the university",<sup id="cite_ref-IHE_2016_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IHE_2016-8">[8]</a></sup> and the validity of the data available globally has been questioned.<sup id="cite_ref-HEPI_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HEPI-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>While some rankings attempt to measure teaching using metrics such as staff to student ratio, the Higher Education Policy Institute has pointed out that the metrics used are more closely related to research than teaching quality, e.g. "Staff to student ratios are an almost direct measure of research activity", and "The proportion of PhD students is also to a large extent an indication of research activity".<sup id="cite_ref-HEPI_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HEPI-5">[5]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Inside_Higher_Ed" title="Inside Higher Ed">Inside Higher Ed</a> similarly states "these criteria do not actually measure teaching, and none even come close to assessing quality of impact".<sup id="cite_ref-IHE_2010_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IHE_2010-4">[4]</a></sup> Many rankings are also considered to contain biases towards the natural sciences and, due to the bibilometric sources used, towards publication in English-language journals.<sup id="cite_ref-IHE_2016_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IHE_2016-8">[8]</a></sup> Some rankings, including ARWU, also fail to make any correction for the sizes of institutions, so a large institution is ranked considerably higher than a small institution with the same quality of research.<sup id="cite_ref-HEPI_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HEPI-5">[5]</a></sup> Other compilers, such as Scimago and <a href="/wiki/U.S._News_and_World_Report" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. News and World Report">U.S. News and World Report</a>, use a mix of size-dependent and size-independent metrics.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some compilers, notably QS, THE and U.S. News, use reputational surveys. The validity of these has been criticised: "Most experts are highly critical of the reliability of simply asking a rather unrandom group of educators and others involved with the academic enterprise for their opinions";<sup id="cite_ref-IHE_2010_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IHE_2010-4">[4]</a></sup> "methodologically [international surveys of reputation] are flawed, effectively they only measure research performance and they skew the results in favour of a small number of institutions."<sup id="cite_ref-HEPI_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HEPI-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>However, despite the criticism, much attention is paid to global rankings, particularly ARWU, QS and THE. Some countries, including Denmark and the Netherlands, use university rankings as part of points-based immigration programmes, while others, such as Russia, automatically recognise degrees from higher-ranked universities. India's <a href="/wiki/University_Grants_Commission_(India)" title="University Grants Commission (India)">University Grants Commission</a> requires foreign partners of Indian universities to be ranked in the top 500 of the THE or ARWU ranking, while Brazil's Science Without Borders programme selected international partner institutions using the THE and QS rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Academic Ranking of World Universities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a></div>
<p>The Academic Ranking of World Universities (ARWU) compiled originally by the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Jiao_Tong_University" title="Shanghai Jiao Tong University">Shanghai Jiao Tong University</a> and now maintained by the ShanghaiRanking Consultancy, has provided annual global rankings of universities since 2003, making it the earliest of its kind. The ranking is funded by the Chinese government and its initial purpose was to measure the gap between Chinese and "world class" universities. In the 2016 Academic Ranking of World Universities there are two Chinese universities (<a href="/wiki/Tsinghua_University" title="Tsinghua University">Tsinghua University</a>, 58th, and <a href="/wiki/Peking_University" title="Peking University">Peking University</a>, 71st) in the first 100 places.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> ARWU rankings have been cited by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i> magazine.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> It has been lauded for being "consistent and transparent" based on an article.<sup id="cite_ref-IHE_2010_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IHE_2010-4">[4]</a></sup> The education ministers of France, Norway and Denmark traveled to China to discuss and find ways to improve their rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> ARWU does not rely on surveys and school submissions. Among other criteria, ARWU includes the number of articles published by <a href="/wiki/Nature_(journal)" title="Nature (journal)"><i>Nature</i></a> or <a href="/wiki/Science_(journal)" title="Science (journal)"><i>Science</i></a> and the number of <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a> winners and <a href="/wiki/Fields_Medal" title="Fields Medal">Fields Medalists</a> (mathematics).<sup id="cite_ref-ARWU_Ranking_Methodology_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARWU_Ranking_Methodology-15">[15]</a></sup> Harvard has topped the ranking for years.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> One of the primary criticisms of ARWU's methodology is that it is biased towards the <a href="/wiki/Natural_science" title="Natural science">natural sciences</a> and English language science journals over other subjects.<sup id="cite_ref-ARWU_Ranking_Methodology_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARWU_Ranking_Methodology-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (June 2017)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup> Moreover, the ARWU is known for "relying solely on research indicators", and "the ranking is heavily weighted toward institutions whose faculty or alumni have won Nobel Prizes": it does not measure "the quality of teaching or the quality of humanities."<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Center_for_World_University_Rankings">Center for World University Rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Center for World University Rankings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>This <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>-based consulting organization has published yearly rankings of world universities since 2012. Rankings are based on quality of education, alumni employment, quality of faculty, number of publications, number of publications in high-quality journals, citations, scientific impact and number of patents.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Eduniversal">Eduniversal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Eduniversal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Eduniversal" title="Eduniversal">Eduniversal</a></div>
<p>This university ranking<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> is owned by the French <a href="/wiki/Consultant" title="Consultant">consulting</a> company and <a href="/wiki/Rating_agency" class="mw-redirect" title="Rating agency">rating agency</a> <i>SMBG</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> It ranks masters and MBA in its 9 geographical regions (the 5 continents).<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="G-factor">G-factor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: G-factor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>G-factor ranks university and college web presence by counting the number of links only from other university websites, using <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> <a href="/wiki/Search_engine" class="mw-redirect" title="Search engine">search engine</a> data. G-factor is an indicator of the popularity or importance of each university's website from the combined perspectives of other institutions. It claims to be an objective peer review of a university through its website—in <a href="/wiki/Social_network_theory" class="mw-redirect" title="Social network theory">social network theory</a> terminology, G-factor measures the centrality of each university's website in the <a href="/wiki/Network_theory" title="Network theory">network</a> of university websites.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_University_Ranking">Global University Ranking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Global University Ranking">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Global University Ranking measures over 400 universities using the RatER, an autonomous, non-commercial, Russian rating agency supported by Russia's academic society.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> The methodology pools universities from ARWU, HEEACT, Times-QS and Webometrics and a pool of experts formed by project officials and managers to determine the rating scales for indicators in seven areas. It considers academic performance, research performance, faculty expertise, resource availability, socially significant activities of graduates, international activities, and international opinion. Each expert independently evaluates these performance indicators for candidate universities. The rating is the average of the expert evaluations.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> This ranking raised questions when it placed Russian <a href="/wiki/Moscow_State_University" title="Moscow State University">Moscow State University</a> in fifth place, ahead of <a href="/wiki/Harvard" class="mw-redirect" title="Harvard">Harvard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Cambridge University">Cambridge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-THE_questions_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THE_questions-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="HEEACT—Ranking_of_Scientific_Papers"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="HEEACT.E2.80.94Ranking_of_Scientific_Papers">HEEACT—Ranking of Scientific Papers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: HEEACT—Ranking of Scientific Papers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/HEEACT_%E2%80%93_Performance_Ranking_of_Scientific_Papers_for_World_Universities" class="mw-redirect" title="HEEACT – Performance Ranking of Scientific Papers for World Universities">HEEACT – Performance Ranking of Scientific Papers for World Universities</a></div>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/40px-Ambox_important.svg.png" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/60px-Ambox_important.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/80px-Ambox_important.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="40" data-file-height="40" /></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text">
<div class="mbox-text-span">This article <b>needs attention from an expert on the subject</b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please add a <i>reason</i> or a <i>talk</i> parameter to this template to explain the issue with the article. Consider <a href="/wiki/Template:Expert_needed" title="Template:Expert needed">associating this request</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject">WikiProject</a>.</span> <small><i>(January 2011)</i></small></div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The Performance Ranking of Scientific Papers for World Universities was produced until 2012 by the <a href="/wiki/Higher_Education_Evaluation_and_Accreditation_Council_of_Taiwan" title="Higher Education Evaluation and Accreditation Council of Taiwan">Higher Education Evaluation and Accreditation Council of Taiwan</a> (HEEACT).<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> The indicators were designed to measure both long-term and short-term research performance of research universities.</p>
<p>This project employed <a href="/wiki/Bibliometrics" title="Bibliometrics">bibliometrics</a> to analyze and rank the performance of the 500 top universities and the top 300 universities in six fields. HEEACT further provides subject rankings in science and technology fields. It also ranked the top 300 universities across ten science and technology fields.<sup id="cite_ref-ranking.heeact.edu.tw_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ranking.heeact.edu.tw-35">[35]</a></sup> The ranking included eight indicators. They were: articles published over prior 11 years; citations of those articles, "current" articles, current citations, average citations, "H-index", number of "highly cited papers" and high impact journal articles. They representedx three criteria of scientific papers performance: research productivity, research impact, and research excellence.</p>
<p>The 2007 ranking methodology was alleged to have favored universities with medical schools, and in response, HEEACT added assessment criteria.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> The six field-based rankings are based on the subject categorization of WOS, including Agriculture &amp; Environment Sciences (AGE), Clinical Medicine (MED), Engineering, Computing &amp; Technology (ENG), Life Sciences (LIFE), Natural Sciences (SCI) and Social Sciences (SOC). The ten subjects include Physics, Chemistry, Mathematics, Geosciences, Electrical Engineering, Computer Science, Mechanical Engineering, Chemical Engineering (including Energy &amp; Fuels), Materials Sciences, and Civil Engineering (including Environmental Engineering).<sup id="cite_ref-ranking.heeact.edu.tw_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ranking.heeact.edu.tw-35">[35]</a></sup> The ranking was renamed as <a href="/wiki/National_Taiwan_University" title="National Taiwan University">National Taiwan University</a> Ranking in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Human_Resources_&amp;_Labor_Review"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_Resources_.26_Labor_Review">Human Resources &amp; Labor Review</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Human Resources &amp; Labor Review">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Human Resources &amp; Labor Review (HRLR) publishes a human competitiveness index &amp; analysis annually by Asia First Media, previously ChaseCareer Network (ChaseCareer.Net). This system is based on Human Resources &amp; Labour Review Indexes (HRI and LRI), which measure the performance of top 300 universities' graduates.<sup id="cite_ref-Asia_First_Media_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Asia_First_Media-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2004, a couple of educational institutions voiced concerns at several events in regard to the accuracy and effectiveness of ranking bodies or lists. The HRLR ranking was pioneered in late 2005 within a working group in response to those concerns. The team was founded in January 2007, in London, and started compiling and processing data, resulting in the first lists in 2007-2008.<sup id="cite_ref-Asia_First_Media_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Asia_First_Media-38">[38]</a></sup> The ranking concept is later being adopted for Alumni score on <a href="/wiki/ARWU" class="mw-redirect" title="ARWU">ARWU</a> and many other rankings.</p>
<p>The new HRLR ranking innovative methods sparked intense interests from many institutions and inspired several other ranking lists and scoring which are based on professional, alumni, executives, competitiveness, human capital-oriented aspects. Nevertheless, HRLR remains to be the leader in university ranking with innovative and comprehensive approaches, and not relying merely on those aforementioned aspects.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="High_Impact_Universities:_Research_Performance_Index">High Impact Universities: Research Performance Index</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: High Impact Universities: Research Performance Index">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The High Impact Universities Research Performance Index (RPI) is a 2010 Australian initiative<sup id="cite_ref-rpi_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rpi-40">[40]</a></sup> that studies university research performance. The pilot project involved a trial of over 1,000 universities or institutions and 5,000 constituent faculties (in various disciplines) worldwide. The top 500 results for universities and faculties were reported at the project website.<sup id="cite_ref-rpi_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rpi-40">[40]</a></sup> The project promotes simplicity, transparency and fairness. The assessment analyzes research performance as measured by publications and citations. Publication and citation data is drawn from <a href="/wiki/Scopus" title="Scopus">Scopus</a>. The project uses standard bibliometric indicators, namely the 10-year <a href="/wiki/G-index" title="G-index">g-index</a> and <a href="/wiki/H-index" title="H-index">h-index</a>. RPI equally weighs contributions from the five faculties. The five faculty scores are <a href="/wiki/Normalization_(statistics)" title="Normalization (statistics)">normalized</a> to place them onto a common scale. The normalized scores are then averaged to arrive at a final RPI.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leiden_Ranking">Leiden Ranking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Leiden Ranking">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/CWTS_Leiden_Ranking" title="CWTS Leiden Ranking">CWTS Leiden Ranking</a></div>
<p>The Centre for Science and Technology Studies at <a href="/wiki/Leiden_University" title="Leiden University">Leiden University</a> maintains a European and worldwide ranking of the top 500 universities according including the number and impact of Web of Science-indexed publications per year. The rankings compare research institutions by taking into account differences in language, discipline and institutional size.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Multiple ranking lists are released according to various bibliometric normalization and impact indicators, including the number of publications, citations-per-publication, and field-averaged impact per publication.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Newsweek">Newsweek</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Newsweek">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In August 2006, the American magazine <a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a> published a ranking of the Top 100 Global Universities, using selected criteria from ARWU and the Times Higher Education-QS rankings, with the additional criterion of the number of volumes in the library. It formed part of a special issue including an article from <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a>, then <a href="/wiki/Prime_minister" title="Prime minister">prime minister</a> of the <a href="/wiki/UK" class="mw-redirect" title="UK">UK</a>, but has not been repeated. It considered openness and diversity as well as distinction in research. The ranking has been continued since its merger with <a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Beast" title="The Daily Beast">The Daily Beast</a>, and currently uses data from the Times Higher Education World Rankings, Webometrics world college rankings from public-research outlet <a href="/wiki/Spanish_National_Research_Council" title="Spanish National Research Council">Consejo Superior de Investigaciones Científicas</a> in <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, and the Shanghai Ranking Consultancy in order to compile its results.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Professional_Ranking_of_World_Universities">Professional Ranking of World Universities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Professional Ranking of World Universities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mines_ParisTech_:_Professional_Ranking_World_Universities" class="mw-redirect" title="Mines ParisTech : Professional Ranking World Universities">Mines ParisTech : Professional Ranking World Universities</a></div>
<p>In contrast to academic rankings, the Professional Ranking of World Universities established in 2007 by the <a href="/wiki/%C3%89cole_nationale_sup%C3%A9rieure_des_mines_de_Paris" class="mw-redirect" title="École nationale supérieure des mines de Paris">École nationale supérieure des mines de Paris</a> measures the efficiency of each university at producing leading business professionals. Its main compilation criterion is the number of <a href="/wiki/Chief_Executive_Officer" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief Executive Officer">Chief Executive Officers</a> (or equivalent) among the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_Global_500" title="Fortune Global 500">Fortune Global 500</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> This ranking has been criticized for placing five French universities into the top 20.<sup id="cite_ref-THE_questions_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THE_questions-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="QS_World_University_Rankings">QS World University Rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: QS World University Rankings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a></div>
<p>The QS World University Rankings are a ranking of the world's top universities produced by <a href="/wiki/Quacquarelli_Symonds" title="Quacquarelli Symonds">Quacquarelli Symonds</a> published annually since 2004. Along with <a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a> and <a href="/wiki/THE_World_University_Rankings" class="mw-redirect" title="THE World University Rankings">THE World University Rankings</a>, the QS World University Rankings is widely recognized and cited as one of the 3 main world university rankings. According to Alexa data, they are the world's most-viewed global university rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> In 2016 they ranked 916 universities, with the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">Massachusetts Institute of Technology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a> on top.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> This represented the first time since the inaugural rankings of 2004 that all three top positions were held by US institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>The QS rankings should not be confused with the <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a>. From 2004 to 2009 the QS rankings were published in collaboration with <i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education" title="Times Higher Education">Times Higher Education</a></i> and were known as the <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education-QS_World_University_Rankings" class="mw-redirect" title="Times Higher Education-QS World University Rankings">Times Higher Education-QS World University Rankings</a>. In 2010 QS assumed sole publication of rankings produced with this methodology when <i>Times Higher Education</i> split from QS in order to create a new rankings methodology in partnership with <a href="/wiki/Thomson_Reuters" title="Thomson Reuters">Thomson Reuters</a>. The QS rankings are published in the United States by <i>U.S. News &amp; World Report</i> as the "World's Best Universities."<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> However, in 2014, the <i>U.S. News &amp; World Report</i> launched their own international university ranking titled "Best Global Universities". The inaugural ranking was published in October 2014.</p>
<p>The QS rankings use peer review data collected (in 2016) from 74,651 scholars and academics and 37,781 recruiters.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> These two indicators are worth 40 per cent and 10 per cent of a university's possible score respectively. The QS rankings also incorporate citation per faculty member data from <a href="/wiki/Scopus" title="Scopus">Scopus</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> faculty/student ratios, and international staff and student numbers. The citations and faculty/student measures are worth 20 per cent of an institution's total possible score and the international staff and student data five per cent each. QS has published online material about its methodology.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>QS published the 2016 <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a> online on 5 September 2016. The rankings also appear in book form, and via media partners including <a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/US_News_%26_World_Report" class="mw-redirect" title="US News &amp; World Report">US News &amp; World Report</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Chosun_Ilbo" title="The Chosun Ilbo">The Chosun Ilbo</a></i>.</p>
<p>QS has added to its main World University Rankings, starting in 2009 with the Asian University Rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> The QS Latin American University Rankings <sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> and the QS World University Rankings by Subject <sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> were published for the first time in 2011, as well as a faculty ranking worldwide,<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Top 50 under 50 and Next 50 under 50 ranking <sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> and graduate employment ranking.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> QS now also publish regional rankings for the Arab Region, Emerging Europe and Central Asia, and the five BRICS nations.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>The subject rankings are intended to address the most frequent criticism of all world university ranking systems, that they contain too little material about specific subjects, something potential applicants are keen to see. These rankings have been drawn up on the basis of citations, academic peer review and recruiter review, with the weightings for each dependent upon the culture and practice of the subject concerned. They are published in five clusters; engineering; biomedicine; the natural sciences; the social sciences; and the arts and humanities, and covered 42 subjects in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="QS_Asian_University_Rankings">QS Asian University Rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: QS Asian University Rankings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 2009, Quacquarelli Symonds (QS) launched a department of the Q<i>S Asian University Rankings</i> in partnership with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Chosun_Ilbo" title="The Chosun Ilbo">The Chosun Ilbo</a></i> newspaper in Korea. They rank the top 350 Asian universities and the ranking has now appeared eight times. They release an independent list of rankings each time, different from that of the QS World University Rankings. For three consecutive years up to the 2016/17 edition, the rankings was topped by the <a href="/wiki/National_University_of_Singapore" title="National University of Singapore">National University of Singapore</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>These rankings use some of the same criteria as the World University Rankings but they use other measures, such as incoming and outgoing exchange students as well. As the criteria and their weightings are different, the QS World university rankings and the QS Asian University rankings released in the same academic year are different.<sup id="cite_ref-vs_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vs-64">[64]</a></sup> QS published global universities ranking by different major in different countries, which has special reference value for international students, like Statistics &amp; Operational Research program in China.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="QS_Latin_American_University_Rankings">QS Latin American University Rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: QS Latin American University Rankings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The QS Latin American University Rankings <sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> were launched in 2011. They use academic opinion (30 per cent), employer opinion (20 per cent), publications per faculty member, citations per paper, academic staff with a PhD, faculty/student ratio and web visibility (10 per cent each) as measures. These criteria were developed in consultation with experts in Latin America, and the web visibility data comes from Webometrics. The 2016/17 edition of the ranking ranks the top 300 universities in the region, and showed that the University of São Paulo in Brazil is the region's top institution.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Reuters_World's_Top_100_Innovative_Universities"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Reuters_World.27s_Top_100_Innovative_Universities">Reuters World's Top 100 Innovative Universities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Reuters World's Top 100 Innovative Universities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The ranking is empirical<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> and compiles a methodology that employs 10 different metrics. The criteria focused on <a href="/wiki/Academic_papers" class="mw-redirect" title="Academic papers">academic papers</a>, which indicate basic research performed at a university, and <a href="/wiki/Patent" title="Patent">patent</a> filings, which point to an institution's interest in protecting and commercializing its discoveries. Compiled by the Intellectual Property &amp; Science business of Thomson Reuters, the list uses proprietary data and analysis tools.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> The process began by identifying the 500 academic and government organizations that published the greatest number of articles in scholarly journals, as indexed in the Thomson Reuters Web of Science Core Collection database. The list was cross referenced against the number of patents filed by each organization during the same time period in the Derwent World Patents Index and the Derwent Innovations Index. Patent equivalents, <a href="/wiki/Citing" class="mw-redirect" title="Citing">citing</a> patents and citing articles were included. The timeframe allows for the articles and patent activity to receive citations, thereby contributing to that portion of the methodology. The list was reduced to just those institutions that filed 70 or more patents, the bulk of which were universities. Each candidate university was then evaluated using various indicators including how often a university's patent applications were granted; how many patents were filed with global patent offices and local authorities; and how often the university's patents were cited by others. Universities were also evaluated in terms of how often their research papers were cited by patents; and the percentage of articles that featured a co-author from industry.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> The ranking has the <a href="/wiki/Asia-Pacific" title="Asia-Pacific">Asia-Pacific</a> edition featuring top 75 institutions across the region <sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> and top 25 most innovative <a href="/wiki/Governmental" class="mw-redirect" title="Governmental">governmental</a> institutions in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Round_University_Ranking">Round University Ranking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Round University Ranking">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Round_University_Ranking" title="Round University Ranking">Round University Ranking</a></div>
<p>Round University Ranking, or abbreviated RUR Rankings is a world university ranking, assessing effectiveness of 750 leading universities in the world based on 20 indicators distributed among 4 key dimension areas: teaching, research, international diversity, financial sustainability. The ranking has international coverage and is intended to become a tool of choice of the university for the key stakeholders of higher education: applicants, students, representatives of the academic community, university management. The RUR Rankings publisher is an independent RUR Rankings Agency,<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> geographically located in Moscow, Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> RUR is aimed to provide transparent, comprehensive analytical system for benchmarking and evaluation universities across the borders to the widest possible audience: students, analysts, decision-makers in the field of higher education development both at individual institutional and at the national level.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="SCImago_Institutions_Rankings">SCImago Institutions Rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: SCImago Institutions Rankings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The SCImago Institutions Rankings (SIR)<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> since 2009 has published its international ranking of worldwide research institutions, the SIR World Report.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> The SIR World Report is the work of the SCImago Research Group,<sup id="cite_ref-sci_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sci-77">[77]</a></sup> a Spain-based research organization consist of members from the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_National_Research_Council" title="Spanish National Research Council">Spanish National Research Council</a> (CSIC), <a href="/wiki/University_of_Granada" title="University of Granada">University of Granada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_III_University_of_Madrid" title="Charles III University of Madrid">Charles III University of Madrid</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alcal%C3%A1" title="University of Alcalá">University of Alcalá</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Extremadura" title="University of Extremadura">University of Extremadura</a> and other education institutions in Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>The ranking measures areas such as: research output, international collaboration, normalized impact and publication rate.<sup id="cite_ref-sci_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sci-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Times Higher Education World University Rankings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a></div>
<p>From 2004 to 2009 <i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education" title="Times Higher Education">Times Higher Education</a></i> (THE), a <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">British</a> publication, published the annual <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education%E2%80%93QS_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education–QS World University Rankings">Times Higher Education–QS World University Rankings</a> in association with <a href="/wiki/Quacquarelli_Symonds" title="Quacquarelli Symonds">Quacquarelli Symonds</a> (QS). THE published a table of the top 200 universities and QS ranked approximately 500 online, in book form, and via media partners.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> On 30 October 2009, THE broke with QS and joined <a href="/wiki/Thomson_Reuters" title="Thomson Reuters">Thomson Reuters</a> to provide a new set of world university rankings, called <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a>. The 2015/16 edition of the Times Higher Education World University Rankings rank the world's 800 best universities, while the 2016/17 instalment will rank the world's top 980.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 3 June 2010, Times Higher Education revealed the methodology which they proposed to use when compiling the new world university rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> The new methodology included 13 separate performance indicators, an increase from the six measures employed between 2004 and 2009. After further consultation the criteria were grouped under five broad overall indicators to produce the final ranking. THE published its first rankings using its new methodology on 16 September 2010, a month earlier than previous years.<sup id="cite_ref-timeshighereducation1_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timeshighereducation1-82">[82]</a></sup> THE also kick-started THE 100 Under 50 ranking<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> and Alma Mater Index.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Globe_and_Mail" title="The Globe and Mail">The Globe and Mail</a></i> in 2010 described the Times Higher Education World University Rankings as "arguably the most influential."<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Research published by professors at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Michigan" title="University of Michigan">University of Michigan</a> in 2011 demonstrated that the early THES rankings were disproportionately influential in establishing the status order of world research universities.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Times_Higher_Education_World_Reputation_Rankings">Times Higher Education World Reputation Rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Times Higher Education World Reputation Rankings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>This ranking was published for the first time in March 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> The 2016 rankings are based on a survey of 10,323 academics from 133 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> They rank <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a> as possessing the world's most powerful university brand, followed by <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">Massachusetts Institute of Technology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> The survey was conducted in eight languages by Ipsos Media CT for Times Higher Education's ranking-data partner Thomson Reuters, and asked experienced academics to highlight what they believed to be the strongest universities for teaching and research in their own fields. The top six universities in the ranking for 2014—<a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">MIT</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">Cambridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford" title="University of Oxford">Oxford</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Berkeley" title="University of California, Berkeley">UC Berkeley</a>—were found to be "head and shoulders above the rest", and were touted as a group of globally recognised "super brands."<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="U-Multirank">U-Multirank</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: U-Multirank">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>U-Multirank, a European Commission supported feasibility study, was undertaken to contribute to the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> objective of enhancing transparency about the different missions and the performance of higher education institutions and research institutes. At a press conference in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a> on 13 May 2011, the U-Multirank was officially launched by <a href="/wiki/Androulla_Vassiliou" title="Androulla Vassiliou">Androulla Vassiliou</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Commissioner_for_Education,_Culture,_Multilingualism_and_Youth" title="European Commissioner for Education, Culture, Multilingualism and Youth">Commissioner for Higher Education and Culture</a> saying: U-Multirank "will be useful to each participating higher education institution, as a planning and self-mapping exercise. By providing students with clearer information to guide their study choices, this is a fresh tool for more quality, relevance and transparency in <a href="/wiki/European_Higher_Education_Area" title="European Higher Education Area">European higher education</a>." <sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> U-Multirank breaks new ground by producing multi-dimensional listings rating universities on a much wider range of factors than existing international rankings. The idea is to avoid simplistic league tables which can result in misleading comparisons between institutions of very different types or mask significant differences in quality between courses at the same university.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>U-Multirank assesses the overall performance of universities but also ranks them in selected academic fields: in 2014 the fields are <a href="/wiki/Business_studies" title="Business studies">business studies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electrical_engineering" title="Electrical engineering">electrical engineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mechanical_engineering" title="Mechanical engineering">mechanical engineering</a> and <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">physics</a>; in 2015, <a href="/wiki/Psychology" title="Psychology">psychology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Computer_science" title="Computer science">computer science</a> and <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">medicine</a> will be added. The universities are tested against up to 30 separate indicators and rated in five performance groups, from 'A' (very good) through 'E' (weak). The results show that while over 95% of institutions achieve an 'A' score on at least one measure, only 12% have more than 10 top scores. Of the 850 universities in the ranking, 62% are from <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, 17% from <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>, 14% from <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> and 7% from <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a> and <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>. U-Multirank received €2 million in <a href="/wiki/EU" class="mw-redirect" title="EU">EU</a> funding from the former <a href="/wiki/Lifelong_Learning_Programme_2007%E2%80%932013" title="Lifelong Learning Programme 2007–2013">Lifelong Learning Programme</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Erasmus_Programme" title="Erasmus Programme">Erasmus</a>) for the years 2013-2015, with the possibility of a further two years of funding in 2015-2017. The goal is for an independent organisation to manage the ranking on a sustainable business model thereafter.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="UniRanks_&quot;The_Ranking_of_Rankings&quot;"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="UniRanks_.22The_Ranking_of_Rankings.22">UniRanks "The Ranking of Rankings"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: UniRanks &quot;The Ranking of Rankings&quot;">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The UniRanks World University Ranking aggregates the results of five global ranking, combining them to form a single rank. It uses the following rankings and weights: THE World University Ranking 22.5%, QS World University Ranking 22.5%, US News Best Global University 22.5%, ARWU 22.5%, Reuters World Top 100 Innovative Universities 10%.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> The first edition of UniRanks was launched in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="University_Ranking_by_Academic_Performance">University Ranking by Academic Performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: University Ranking by Academic Performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/University_Ranking_by_Academic_Performance" title="University Ranking by Academic Performance">University Ranking by Academic Performance</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/University_Ranking_by_Academic_Performance" title="University Ranking by Academic Performance">University Ranking by Academic Performance</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-urapweb_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-urapweb-99">[99]</a></sup> abbreviated as URAP, was developed in the Informatics Institute<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> of <a href="/wiki/Middle_East_Technical_University" title="Middle East Technical University">Middle East Technical University</a>. Since 2010, it has been publishing annual national and global<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> college and university rankings for top 2000 institutions. The <a href="/wiki/Scientometrics" title="Scientometrics">scientometrics</a> measurement of URAP is based on data obtained from the <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Scientific_Information" title="Institute for Scientific Information">Institute for Scientific Information</a> via <a href="/wiki/Web_of_Science" title="Web of Science">Web of Science</a> and inCites. For global rankings, URAP employs indicators of research performance including the number of articles, citation, total documents, article impact total, citation impact total, and international collaboration. In addition to global rankings, URAP publishes regional rankings for universities in <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> using additional indicators such as the number of students and faculty members obtained from Center of Measuring, Selection and Placement <a href="/wiki/%C3%96SYM" class="mw-redirect" title="ÖSYM">ÖSYM</a>.</p>
<h3><span id="U.S._News_&amp;_World_Report's_Best_Global_Universities_Rankings"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="U.S._News_.26_World_Report.27s_Best_Global_Universities_Rankings">U.S. News &amp; World Report's Best Global Universities Rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: U.S. News &amp; World Report's Best Global Universities Rankings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report_Best_Global_University_Ranking" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report Best Global University Ranking">U.S. News &amp; World Report Best Global University Ranking</a></div>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a>'</i>s inaugural Best Global Universities ranking<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> was launched on 28 October 2014, and it was based on data and metrics provided by <a href="/wiki/Thomson_Reuters" title="Thomson Reuters">Thomson Reuters</a>, and are thus methodologically different from the criteria traditionally used by <i>U.S. News</i> to rank American institutions. Universities are judged on factors such as global research reputation, publications and number of highly cited papers.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> <i>U.S. News</i> also publishes region-specific and subject-specific global rankings based on this methodology.</p>
<p>The annual U.S. News Best Global Universities rankings were produced to provide insight into how universities compare globally. As an increasing number of students are planning to enroll in universities outside of their own country, the Best Global Universities rankings – which focus specifically on schools' academic research and reputation overall and not on their separate undergraduate or graduate programs – can help those students accurately compare institutions around the world.</p>
<p>The Best Global Universities rankings also provide insight into how U.S. universities – which U.S. News has been ranking separately for more than 30 years – stand globally. All universities can now benchmark themselves against schools in their own country and region, become more visible on the world stage and find top schools in other countries to consider collaborating with.</p>
<p>The overall Best Global Universities rankings encompass the top 750 institutions spread out across 57 countries – up from the top 500 universities in 49 countries ranked last year. The first step in producing these rankings, which are powered by Thomson Reuters InCitesTM research analytics solutions, involved creating a pool of 1,000 universities that was used to rank the top 750 schools.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> In comparison with US News National University Ranking.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> the Global University Ranking is focused on the research power and faculty resources for students, while the National Ranking is only focused on undergraduate studies. Therefore, for graduate studies and international students, the Best Global Universities Ranking is a much better reference than National University Ranking.</p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Inside_Higher_Ed" title="Inside Higher Ed">Inside Higher Ed</a></i> noted that the <i>U.S. News</i> is entering into the international college and university rankings area that is already "dominated by three major global university rankings": the <i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a></i>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a></i>, and the <i><a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-HigherEd_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HigherEd-106">[106]</a></sup> <i>U.S. News'</i>s chief data strategist Robert Morse stated "We're well-known in the field for doing academic rankings so we thought it was a natural extension of the other rankings that we're doing."<sup id="cite_ref-HigherEd_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HigherEd-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p>Morse pointed out that the <i>U.S. News</i> as "the first American publisher to enter the global rankings space", given <i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education" title="Times Higher Education">Times Higher Education</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Quacquarelli_Symonds" title="Quacquarelli Symonds">QS</a> are both British, while the Academic Ranking of World universities is Chinese.<sup id="cite_ref-HigherEd_106-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HigherEd-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Webometrics">Webometrics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Webometrics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Webometrics_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Webometrics Ranking of World Universities">Webometrics Ranking of World Universities</a></div>
<p>The Webometrics Ranking of World Universities is produced by Cybermetrics Lab (CCHS), a unit of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_National_Research_Council" title="Spanish National Research Council">Spanish National Research Council</a> (CSIC), the main public research body in Spain. It offers information about more than 12,000 universities according to their web presence (an assessment of the scholarly contents, visibility and impact of universities on the web). The ranking is updated every January and July.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Webometrics" title="Webometrics">Webometrics</a> Ranking or Ranking Web is built from a database of over 20,000 higher education institutions. The top 12,000 universities are shown in the main ranking and more are covered in regional lists.</p>
<p>The ranking started in 2004 and is based on a composite indicator that includes both the volume of the Web contents and the visibility and impact of web publications according to the number of external links they received. A wide range of scientific activities appears exclusively on academic websites and is typically overlooked by bibliometric indicators.</p>
<p>Webometric indicators measure institutional commitment to Web publication. Webometric results show a high correlation with other rankings. However, North American universities are relatively common in the top 200, while small and medium-size biomedical institutions and German, French, Italian and Japanese universities were less common in the top ranks. Possible reasons include publishing via independent research councils (CNRS, Max Planck, CNR) or the large amount of non-English web contents, which are less likely to be linked.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wuhan_University">Wuhan University</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Wuhan University">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Research Center for Chinese Science Evaluation at <a href="/wiki/Wuhan_University" title="Wuhan University">Wuhan University</a> ranking is based on Essential Science Indicators (ESI), which provides data on journal article publication counts and citation frequencies in over 11,000 journals around the world in 22 research fields.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Regional_and_national_rankings">Regional and national rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Regional and national rankings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Regional and national rankings are carried out in Africa, Asia, Europe, North America, South America and Oceania.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia">Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>QS's Asian University Rankings<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> use some of the same data as the QS World University Rankings alongside other material, such as the number of exchange students attending or traveling from each university. The rankings list the top 350 universities in Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="China">China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/University_rankings_in_China" title="University rankings in China">University rankings in China</a></div>
<p>University rankings in China are ordered by different standards and made by various organizations, including:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chinese_university_ranking_(Wu_Shulian)" title="Chinese university ranking (Wu Shulian)">Wu Shulian</a>, published in the name of the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Academy_of_Management_Science" title="Chinese Academy of Management Science">Chinese Academy of Management Science</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chinese_university_ranking_(Netbig)" title="Chinese university ranking (Netbig)">Netbig</a>, the higher education internet information company</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chinese_university_ranking_(CUAA)" title="Chinese university ranking (CUAA)">CUAA</a>, by Airuishen (a company) in the name of Chinese Universities Alumni Association, etc.</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/w/index.php?title=Medical_College_Ranking_India_2015&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Medical College Ranking India 2015 (page does not exist)">Medical College Ranking India 2015</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Institutional_Ranking_Framework" title="National Institutional Ranking Framework">National Institutional Ranking Framework</a> is initiated by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Human_Resource_Development" title="Ministry of Human Resource Development">Ministry of Human Resource Development</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India" title="Government of India">Government of India</a>, to rank all <a href="/wiki/Institutions_of_higher_education" class="mw-redirect" title="Institutions of higher education">institutions of higher education</a> in India. Magazines such as Youth Incorporated,<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-110">[110]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/India_Today" title="India Today">India Today</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Outlook_(magazine)" title="Outlook (magazine)">Outlook</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Mint_(newspaper)" title="Mint (newspaper)">Mint</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Week_(Indian_magazine)" title="The Week (Indian magazine)">The Week</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Dataquest" title="Dataquest">Dataquest</a></i>, <i>Careers360</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Electronics_For_You" class="mw-redirect" title="Electronics For You">Electronics For You</a></i> conduct <a href="/wiki/Template:Infobox_India_university_ranking" title="Template:Infobox India university ranking">annual rankings</a> for the major disciplines.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Japan">Japan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Japan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Most of the ranking systems in Japan rank universities by the difficulty of their entrance exams, called "<a href="/wiki/Standard_score" title="Standard score">Hensachi</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> One example of such a ranking is <a href="/wiki/Going_broke_universities_-_Disappearing_universities" class="mw-redirect" title="Going broke universities - Disappearing universities">Going broke universities - Disappearing universities</a> by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiyoshi_Shimano&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kiyoshi Shimano (page does not exist)">Kiyoshi Shimano</a><sup class="noprint" style="font-style: normal;">[<a href="https://ja.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E5%B3%B6%E9%87%8E%E6%B8%85%E5%BF%97" class="extiw" title="ja:島野清志">ja</a>]</sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-GBUDU1_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GBUDU1-112">[112]</a></sup> Organizations who use other methods of ranking universities in Japan include <a href="/wiki/Nikkei_Business_Publications" title="Nikkei Business Publications">Nikkei Business Publications</a>, which annually releases the <a href="/wiki/Brand_rankings_of_Japanese_universities" title="Brand rankings of Japanese universities">Brand rankings of Japanese universities</a> every November. <a href="/wiki/Toyo_Keizai" title="Toyo Keizai">Toyo Keizai</a>, who regularly releases the university rankings "<a href="/wiki/Truly_Strong_Universities" title="Truly Strong Universities">Truly Strong Universities</a>" once a year, is another example.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> Japanese leading prep school <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kawaijuku&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kawaijuku (page does not exist)">Kawaijuku</a><sup class="noprint" style="font-style: normal;">[<a href="https://ja.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E6%B2%B3%E5%90%88%E5%A1%BE" class="extiw" title="ja:河合塾">ja</a>]</sup> also released the Japan's Top 30 University Rankings in Natural Sciences and Technology for <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Education,_Culture,_Sports,_Science_and_Technology" title="Ministry of Education, Culture, Sports, Science and Technology">MEXT</a>'s <a href="/w/index.php?title=GLOBAL_30_Project&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="GLOBAL 30 Project (page does not exist)">GLOBAL 30 Project</a><sup class="noprint" style="font-style: normal;">[<a href="https://ja.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E5%9B%BD%E9%9A%9B%E5%8C%96%E6%8B%A0%E7%82%B9%E6%95%B4%E5%82%99%E4%BA%8B%E6%A5%AD" class="extiw" title="ja:国際化拠点整備事業">ja</a>]</sup> in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pakistan">Pakistan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Pakistan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rankings_of_universities_in_Pakistan" title="Rankings of universities in Pakistan">Rankings of universities in Pakistan</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Higher_Education_Commission_(Pakistan)" class="mw-redirect" title="Higher Education Commission (Pakistan)">Higher Education Commission</a> annually ranks domestic universities.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Philippines">Philippines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Philippines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Higher_education_in_the_Philippines" title="Higher education in the Philippines">Higher education in the Philippines</a></div>
<p>Academic rankings in the Philippines are conducted by the <a href="/wiki/Professional_Regulation_Commission" title="Professional Regulation Commission">Professional Regulation Commission</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Commission_on_Higher_Education_(Philippines)" title="Commission on Higher Education (Philippines)">Commission on Higher Education</a>, based on the average passing rates in board tests.,<sup id="cite_ref-phil_rank_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-phil_rank-118">[118]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-up_news_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-up_news-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Korea">South Korea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: South Korea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Korean Council for University Education, established in 2009, evaluates universities in South Korea.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Union">European Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: European Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> compiled a list of the 22 universities in the EU with the highest scientific impact.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> This ranking was compiled as part of the Third European Report on Science &amp; Technology Indicators,<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> prepared by the Directorate General for Science and Research of the European Commission in 2003 (updated 2004).<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> It only explicitly considers the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>'s top institutions, but comparisons with the rest of the world are provided in the full report. The report says, "University College London comes out on top in both publications (the number of scientific publications produced by the university) and citations (the number of times those scientific publications are cited by other researchers)" however the table lists the top scoring university as "Univ London" implying that the authors counted the scientific output of the entire <a href="/wiki/University_of_London" title="University of London">University of London</a>, rather than its constituent colleges.</p>
