<p>In this ranking, the EU's top two universities are <a href="/wiki/Cambridge" title="Cambridge">Cambridge</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oxford" title="Oxford">Oxford</a>, as in the Jiao Tong and Times rankings. This ranking stresses the scientific quality of the institution, as opposed to its size or perceived prestige.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Thus smaller, technical universities, such as <a href="/wiki/Eindhoven_University_of_Technology" title="Eindhoven University of Technology">Eindhoven</a> (Netherlands) and the <a href="/wiki/Technical_University_Munich" class="mw-redirect" title="Technical University Munich">Technical University Munich</a> (Germany) are ranked third and fourth, behind Cambridge, and followed by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Edinburgh" title="University of Edinburgh">University of Edinburgh</a>. The report does not provide a direct comparison between EU and universities in the rest of the world, although it does compute a scientific impact score, which is measured against the world average.</p>
<p>In December 2008, the European Commission published a call for tenders, inviting bidders to design and test a new multi-dimensional university ranking system with global outreach. The first results of the envisaged pilot project were promised for the first half of 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<p>Another approach to classify the European research area is offered by 'European Research Ranking'.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> This ranking is based on publicly available data from the European Commissions project and funding database CORDIS to estimate the funding and networking performance of European research institutions.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Austria">Austria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Austria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Some Austrian universities, including all Austrian Universities of Applied Sciences, take part in the CHE University Ranking.<sup id="cite_ref-view_CHE_UniversityRanking_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-view_CHE_UniversityRanking-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Bulgaria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Bulgarian University Ranking System, maintained by the Bulgarian Ministry of Education, compares academic programs in accredited domestic higher education institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> The system ranks programs based on more than 50 indicators, such as teaching and learning conditions, scientific research, career development opportunities, prestige, and material resources.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Denmark">Denmark</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Denmark">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In Denmark, the think-tank <a href="/wiki/CEPOS" title="CEPOS">CEPOS</a> conduct an annual survey and ranking of higher education at study program level and institution level, based on entry salary, career development, drop-out rates, and program completion rates.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="France">France</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: France">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Eduniversal" title="Eduniversal">Eduniversal</a></i> provides rankings of undergraduate and graduate degrees of French universities in some areas.</p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Le_Nouvel_Observateur" class="mw-redirect" title="Le Nouvel Observateur">Le Nouvel Observateur</a></i> occasionally offer rankings of "<i><a href="/wiki/Grandes_%C3%A9coles" title="Grandes écoles">Grandes écoles</a></i>" and their preparatory schools, the "<i>Prépas</i>", and of universities’ undergraduate degrees in some areas.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Germany">Germany</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Germany">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Since 2007, the CHE "ExcellenceRanking" has been published by the Center for Higher Education Development in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-129">[129]</a></sup> The ranking includes the sciences of biology, chemistry, mathematics and physics as well as psychology, political science and economics. The ranking is designed to support the search for masters or doctoral programmes. The CHE also wants to highlight the research strengths of European universities and provide them with ideas for improvement. The ranking is published by the German weekly newspaper <a href="/wiki/Die_Zeit" title="Die Zeit">Die Zeit</a> in English and German. The CHE Center for Higher Education Development gathers the data for this ranking. An English version is provided by the <a href="/wiki/German_Academic_Exchange_Service" title="German Academic Exchange Service">DAAD</a>.</p>
<p>The CHE also publishes a "ResearchRanking" showing the research strengths of German universities. The CHE ResearchRanking is based on the research-related data of the UniversityRanking.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ireland">Ireland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Ireland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Sunday_Times_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Sunday Times (UK)">The Sunday Times</a></i> ranks Irish universities based on a mix of criteria, including secondary school examination scores, graduation rates, staff-student ratio, research efficiency, accommodation, nontraditional students, athletics and sports facilities.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Italy">Italy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Italy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Every year, the newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/La_Repubblica" title="La Repubblica">La Repubblica</a></i>, in collaboration with <a href="/w/index.php?title=CENSIS&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="CENSIS (page does not exist)">CENSIS</a>, compiles a ranking of Italian universities.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Macedonia">Macedonia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Macedonia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a> (ARWU) compiled a ranking of Macedonian Higher Education Institutions (HEIs) commissioned by the country's Ministry of Education and Science in February 2011 and released it on 16 February 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> Nineteen qualified HEIs were included in the ranking. The ranking used 19 indicators of academic performance and competitiveness, covering major mission aspects of HEIs such as teaching, research and social service. It is the first university ranking in Macedonia.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Netherlands">Netherlands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Netherlands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Most Dutch universities take part in the CHE UniversityRanking.<sup id="cite_ref-view_CHE_UniversityRanking_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-view_CHE_UniversityRanking-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Poland">Poland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Poland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A popular ranking of Polish higher education institutions is annually published by education magazine <i>Perspektywy</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Perspektywy_magazine_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Perspektywy_magazine-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Romania">Romania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Romania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Ad Astra association of Romanian scientists ranked Romanian universities in 2006 and 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-Ad_Astra_ranking_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ad_Astra_ranking-135">[135]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Russian_Federation">Russian Federation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Russian Federation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Several bodies rank Russian universities, including <a href="/wiki/RIA_Novosti" title="RIA Novosti">RIA Novosti</a> / <a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a>, independent rating agency RatER, <a href="/wiki/Interfax" title="Interfax">Interfax</a> (in cooperation with <a href="/wiki/Ekho_Moskvy" class="mw-redirect" title="Ekho Moskvy">Ekho Moskvy</a>) and the Russian journal <i>Finance</i>.</p>
<p>RIA Novosty / Forbes rankings are conducted under the supervision of <a href="/wiki/Public_Chamber_of_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Public Chamber of Russia">Public Chamber of Russia</a> in cooperation with <a href="/wiki/State_University_%E2%80%93_Higher_School_of_Economics" class="mw-redirect" title="State University – Higher School of Economics">State University – Higher School of Economics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rian.ru_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rian.ru-136">[136]</a></sup> This ranking is considered the most objective system.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> It covers 476 higher education institutions and is based on the average score of the Unified State Examination that is required to enter a university. The ranking has separate subrankings for different subjects and clusters of universities.</p>
<p>RIA Novosty rankings do not align with other local and international rankings such as <a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a> and <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a> which take into account inherited reputation from the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rian.ru_136-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rian.ru-136">[136]</a></sup></p>
<p>RatER publishes annual rankings based on representation of university graduates in governmental, education and business elite.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p>Interfax annually ranks "classical" (or multi-faculty) universities and higher education institutions specialising in <a href="/wiki/Law_school" title="Law school">law</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> Interfax' methodology <i>quantifies</i> several <i>qualitative</i> factors such as research, teaching standards, public opinion and social and international activity.</p>
<p><i>Finance</i> produces an integrated ranking of higher education institutions specialising in economics and finance.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> The Journal uses the average score of the Unified State Examination, the number of <a href="/wiki/CFO" class="mw-redirect" title="CFO">CFO</a> graduates and the consolidated turnover of companies where graduate CFOs are employed.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sweden">Sweden</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Sweden">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In Sweden, the Confederation of Swedish Enterprise (Svenskt Näringsliv) conduct an annual survey and ranking of higher education at study program level, based on entry salary, career development, internationalization, and degree of academic-business collaboration.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Switzerland">Switzerland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Switzerland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The swissUp Ranking ranked Swiss university and polytechnic students until 2004. The swissUp Ranking is no longer conducted. Some universities from the German-speaking part of Switzerland, such as <a href="/w/index.php?title=ISFOA&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="ISFOA (page does not exist)">ISFOA</a> Lugano take part in the CHE UniversityRanking.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ukraine">Ukraine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Ukraine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>'s Ministry of Education and Science performs official yearly university evaluations.<sup id="cite_ref-Ministry_Ukraine_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ministry_Ukraine-141">[141]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Zerkalo_Nedeli" title="Zerkalo Nedeli">Zerkalo Nedeli</a> newspaper published the top 200–ranked Ukrainian universities in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-RankZN_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RankZN-142">[142]</a></sup> Kyiv Student Council ranks universities on criteria of student satisfaction.<sup id="cite_ref-Kyiv_Student_Council_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kyiv_Student_Council-143">[143]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rankings_of_universities_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Rankings of universities in the United Kingdom">Rankings of universities in the United Kingdom</a></div>
<p>There are three major rankings of universities in the United Kingdom published by commercial companies: The Times and Sunday Times Good University Guide, <a href="/wiki/The_Complete_University_Guide" class="mw-redirect" title="The Complete University Guide">The Complete University Guide</a> and the Guardian University Guide.<sup id="cite_ref-University_guide_2012_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-University_guide_2012-144">[144]</a></sup> Since 2008, <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education" title="Times Higher Education">Times Higher Education</a> has compiled a 'Table of Tables'<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> which combines the results of the 3 national league tables. For 2017, the top 5 universities were <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Cambridge University">Cambridge University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oxford_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Oxford University">Oxford University</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_St_Andrews" title="University of St Andrews">University of St Andrews</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Imperial_College_London" title="Imperial College London">Imperial College London</a> and <a href="/wiki/Durham_University" title="Durham University">Durham University</a> in joint fourth.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Research_Excellence_Framework" title="Research Excellence Framework">Research Excellence Framework</a> was the successor to the <a href="/wiki/Research_Assessment_Exercise" title="Research Assessment Exercise">Research Assessment Exercise</a> in 2014. It is used by the UK government to evaluate the research quality of British universities and determine the distribution of future research funding. In 2014, the top five universities for research power as compiled by <a href="/wiki/Research_Fortnight" title="Research Fortnight">Research Fortnight</a> were <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford" title="University of Oxford">University of Oxford</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_College_London" title="University College London">University College London</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">University of Cambridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Edinburgh" title="University of Edinburgh">University of Edinburgh</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Manchester" title="University of Manchester">University of Manchester</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Research_Assessment_Exercise" title="Research Assessment Exercise">Research Assessment Exercises</a> (RAE) were the UK government's evaluation of research quality in British Universities. Each subject, called a unit of assessment, was ranked by a peer review panel. The rankings were used in the allocation of government funding. The last assessment was made in 2008. The RAE provided quality ratings for research across all disciplines. Panels used a standard scale for each submission. Ratings ranged from 1 to 5, according to the quantity of work that was judged to reach national or international levels of excellence. Participating institutions receive grants from one of the four higher education funding bodies in England, Scotland, Wales and Northern Ireland. The top three universities in the 2008 RAE exercise were <a href="/wiki/London_School_of_Economics" title="London School of Economics">London School of Economics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Cambridge University">Cambridge University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oxford_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Oxford University">Oxford University</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Quality_Assurance_Agency_for_Higher_Education" title="Quality Assurance Agency for Higher Education">Quality Assurance Agency for Higher Education</a> (QAA) assesses undergraduate teaching. QAA is an independent body established by the UK's higher education institutions in 1997. QAA was under contract to the <a href="/wiki/Higher_Education_Funding_Council_for_England" title="Higher Education Funding Council for England">Higher Education Funding Council for England</a> to assess quality for English universities. This replaced Teaching Quality Assessments (TQAs) which aimed to assess the administrative, policy and procedural framework within which teaching took place and did not directly assess teaching quality. This inspection-based system was replaced by a system of information provision, including a national student survey. QAA publishes scores which have been used by the <a href="/wiki/League_table" class="mw-redirect" title="League table">league table</a> industry. The first <a href="/wiki/Teaching_Excellence_Framework" title="Teaching Excellence Framework">Teaching Excellence Framework</a> is to be published in 2017; this is a rating system (giving gold, silver or bronze ratings to higher education providers) rather than a ranking as such.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_America">North America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: North America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rankings_of_universities_in_Canada" title="Rankings of universities in Canada">Rankings of universities in Canada</a></div>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Maclean%27s" title="Maclean's">Maclean's</a></i>, a Canadian news magazine, publishes an annual ranking of Canadian Universities, called the <a href="/wiki/Maclean%27s_University_Rankings#Maclean.27s_Guide_to_Canadian_Universities" class="mw-redirect" title="Maclean's University Rankings">Maclean's University Rankings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> Ranking criteria include student body characteristics, classes, faculty, finances, library, and reputation. The rankings are split into three categories: schools that focus on undergraduate studies with few to no graduate programs, schools that have both extensive undergraduate studies and an extensive selection of graduate programs and schools that have a professional medical program and a selection of graduate programs.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Calgary" title="University of Calgary">University of Calgary</a> produced a formal study examining the ranking methodology, illuminating the factors that determined its rank and criticizing certain aspects of the methodology. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alberta" title="University of Alberta">University of Alberta</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto" title="University of Toronto">University of Toronto</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Manitoba" title="University of Manitoba">University of Manitoba</a> have expressed displeasure over the ranking system.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup></p>
<p>A notable difference between rankings in the United States and <i>Maclean's</i> rankings, however, is that <i>Maclean's</i> excludes privately funded universities. However, the majority of Canada's institutions, including the best-known, are publicly funded.</p>
<p>Beginning in September 2006, over 20 Canadian universities, including several of the most prestigious and largest universities such as the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto" title="University of Toronto">University of Toronto</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_British_Columbia" title="University of British Columbia">University of British Columbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alberta" title="University of Alberta">University of Alberta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Concordia_University_(Quebec)" class="mw-redirect" title="Concordia University (Quebec)">Concordia University</a>, <a href="/wiki/McMaster_University" title="McMaster University">McMaster University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dalhousie_University" title="Dalhousie University">Dalhousie University</a>, jointly refused to participate.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alberta" title="University of Alberta">University of Alberta</a> president <a href="/wiki/Indira_Samarasekera" title="Indira Samarasekera">Indira Samarasekera</a> wrote that <i>Maclean's</i> initially filed a "<a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_information_in_Canada" title="Freedom of information in Canada">Freedom of Information</a>" request but that it was "too late" for the universities to respond. Samarasekera further stated, "Most of [the universities] had already posted the data online, and we directed <i>Maclean's</i> staff to our Web sites. In instances where the magazine staff couldn't find data on our Web site, they chose to use the previous year's data."<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mexico">Mexico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Mexico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Academic_rankings_of_universities_in_Mexico" title="Academic rankings of universities in Mexico">Academic rankings of universities in Mexico</a></div>
<h5><span id="Estudio_Comparativo_de_Universidades_Mexicanas_(ECUM)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Estudio_Comparativo_de_Universidades_Mexicanas_.28ECUM.29">Estudio Comparativo de Universidades Mexicanas (ECUM)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Estudio Comparativo de Universidades Mexicanas (ECUM)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Universities_Comparative_Study" title="Mexican Universities Comparative Study">Mexican Universities Comparative Study</a></div>
<p>Mexican institutions have been compared in the <i>Estudio Comparativo de Universidades Mexicanas</i> (ECUM) produced within the <a href="/wiki/Universidad_Nacional_Aut%C3%B3noma_de_M%C3%A9xico" class="mw-redirect" title="Universidad Nacional Autónoma de México">Universidad Nacional Autónoma de México</a> (UNAM).<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> ECUM provides data on institutional participation in articles on <a href="/wiki/ISI_Web_of_Knowledge" class="mw-redirect" title="ISI Web of Knowledge">ISI Web of Knowledge</a>–indexed journals; faculty participation in each of Mexico's three-level National Researchers System (SNI<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup>); graduate degrees within National Council of Science and Technology's (<a href="/wiki/CONACYT" class="mw-redirect" title="CONACYT">CONACYT</a>) register of quality graduate programs;<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> and number of academic research bodies (<i>cuerpos academicos</i>) according to the <a href="/wiki/Secretariat_of_Public_Education" class="mw-redirect" title="Secretariat of Public Education">Secretariat of Public Education</a> (SEP) program PROMEP.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup></p>
<p>ECUM provides online access to data for 2007 and 2008 through ExECUM.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> Institutional data can be visualized through three options:</p>
<ul>
<li>A selection of the most prominent 58 universities (43 publics and 13 privates). This selection accounts for more than 60 percent of undergraduate and graduate enrollments. It includes public federal universities (<a href="/wiki/UNAM" class="mw-redirect" title="UNAM">UNAM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Instituto_Polit%C3%A9cnico_Nacional" title="Instituto Politécnico Nacional">Instituto Politécnico Nacional</a>, <a href="/wiki/Universidad_Aut%C3%B3noma_Metropolitana" title="Universidad Autónoma Metropolitana">Universidad Autónoma Metropolitana</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Pedagogic_University_(Mexico)" title="National Pedagogic University (Mexico)">Universidad Pedagógica Nacional</a>, Universidad del Ejército y la Fuerza Aérea, <a href="/wiki/Colegio_de_M%C3%A9xico" class="mw-redirect" title="Colegio de México">Colegio de México</a>, <a href="/wiki/Universidad_Aut%C3%B3noma_de_Chapingo" class="mw-redirect" title="Universidad Autónoma de Chapingo">Universidad Autónoma de Chapingo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Universidad_Aut%C3%B3noma_Agraria_Antonio_Narro" title="Universidad Autónoma Agraria Antonio Narro">Universidad Autónoma Agraria Antonio Narro</a>); 35 public state universities (UPES), and a group of private institutions that feature within ECUM's selected classification data.</li>
<li>Result tables for the top 20 institutions in each of the data labels in this study. These include some of the selected universities in addition to the rest of Mexico's higher education institutions, as well as institutes, centers and other research producing organizations.</li>
<li>A personalized selection from more than 600 institutions. These are classified by institutional type, institutional gatherings, by activity sector alphabetically.</li>
</ul>
<p>ExECUM allows users to establish comparison types and levels which they consider relevant. Data is presented in raw form with virtually no derived indicators. Users can relate variables and build indicators according to their own analytical perspectives.</p>
<p>Based on this comparative study project, ECUM's creator, the Dirección General de Evaluación Institucional, published reports providing an analysis of the data for 2007 and 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rankings_of_universities_in_the_United_States" title="Rankings of universities in the United States">Rankings of universities in the United States</a></div>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Council_for_Aid_to_Education">Council for Aid to Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Council for Aid to Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The Council for Aid to Education publishes a list of the top universities in terms of annual fundraising. Fundraising ability reflects, among other things, alumni and outside donor's views of the quality of a university, as well as the ability of that university to expend funds on top faculty and facilities. Most recent rankings put Stanford at the top, ahead of Harvard and Columbia.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span id="The_Daily_Beast's_Guide_to_the_Best_Colleges"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Daily_Beast.27s_Guide_to_the_Best_Colleges">The Daily Beast's Guide to the Best Colleges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: The Daily Beast's Guide to the Best Colleges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The Daily Beast's college rankings take into account nine factors, with future earnings, affordability, and graduation rate weighted most heavily. The other criteria include academics, diversity, athletics, nightlife, activities, and campus quality. The Daily Beast's college rankings took into account approximately 2000 colleges and reported the top 200 scoring schools. The Daily Beast's college rankings report the top 250 scoring schools, with Stanford University at the top, followed by Harvard University, Yale University, MIT, and Columbia University.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span id="The_Economist's_&quot;Best_Colleges._The_Value_of_University&quot;"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Economist.27s_.22Best_Colleges._The_Value_of_University.22"><i>The Economist'</i>s "Best Colleges. The Value of University"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: The Economist's &quot;Best Colleges. The Value of University&quot;">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Economist (magazine)">The Economist</a>'</i>s college rankings <a href="/wiki/The_Economist_Magazine%27s_List_of_America%27s_Best_Colleges" title="The Economist Magazine's List of America's Best Colleges">The Economist Magazine's List of America's Best Colleges</a> focuses on comparable economical advantages defined as 'the economic value of a university is equal to the gap between how much its students subsequently earn, and how much they might have made had they studied elsewhere'.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> Based on set of strict criteria sourced from U.S. Department of Education ('College Scorecard") with relevant 'expected earnings' and multiple statistics applied in calculation of 'median earnings' conclusive evaluation method has been applied to run the scorecard's earnings data through a multiple regression analysis, a common method of measuring the relationships between variables.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Forbes_College_rankings">Forbes College rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=61" title="Edit section: Forbes College rankings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>In 2008, <a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes.com</a> began publishing an annual list, prepared by the <i>Center for College Affordability and Productivity</i><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> of "America's Best Colleges".<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><b>Student satisfaction</b> (evaluations from <a href="/wiki/RateMyProfessors.com" title="RateMyProfessors.com">RateMyProfessors.com</a>, <a href="/wiki/Retention_rate" title="Retention rate">retention rates</a> and targeted student satisfaction surveys on <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a>) constitutes 25% of the score.</li>
<li><b>Post-graduate success</b> (self-reported salaries of alumni from <a href="/wiki/PayScale" title="PayScale">PayScale</a>, alumni appearing on the CCAP's <i>America's Leaders List</i>) constitutes 32.5% of the score.</li>
<li><b>Student debt loads</b> constitute 25% of the score.</li>
<li><b>Graduation rate</b> (the proportion of students who complete four-year degrees in four years) constitutes 7.5% of the score.</li>
<li><b>Academic success</b> (the proportion of students receiving nationally competitive awards) constitutes 10% of the score. Public <a href="/wiki/Reputation" title="Reputation">reputation</a> is not considered, which causes some colleges to score lower than in other lists. A three-year <a href="/wiki/Moving_average" title="Moving average">moving average</a> is used to smooth out the scoring.</li>
</ul>
<p>The 2016 ranking put Stanford at the top, followed by Williams, Princeton, Harvard, and MIT.</p>
<h5><span id="The_&quot;Objective&quot;_College_rankings"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_.22Objective.22_College_rankings">The "Objective" College rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=62" title="Edit section: The &quot;Objective&quot; College rankings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>In 2015, a new website began publishing what it terms The Objective College Ranking.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> The ranking is based on objectively measurable data about US colleges from The <a href="/wiki/National_Center_for_Education_Statistics" title="National Center for Education Statistics">National Center for Education Statistics</a> - the weighting factors for different college metrics are given on the site for transparency. Interestingly, refreshing the webpage changes the ranking, showing how sensitive any college ranking process is to the weighting given different factors. While this site is clearly satirical in nature, it makes a profound point regarding the ultimate subjectivity of all college ranking methods.</p>
<h5><span id="Money's_Best_Colleges"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Money.27s_Best_Colleges">Money's Best Colleges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=63" title="Edit section: Money's Best Colleges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Money magazine's college rankings take into account 21 factors which it categorizes as measures of educational quality, affordability, and alumni earnings. The rankings considered 1500 four-year colleges and reported the top ranking 736. In 2015, according to Money, the top five colleges are Stanford, Babson, MIT, Princeton, and Caltech.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Princeton_Review_Dream_Colleges">The Princeton Review Dream Colleges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=64" title="Edit section: The Princeton Review Dream Colleges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The Princeton Review annually asks students and parents what their dream college is, if cost and ability to get in were not factors. In 2016, for the fourth consecutive year, Stanford was the top "dream school" for both students and parents. Second and third places, in 2016, were taken by Harvard and New York University among students, and Harvard and Princeton among parents.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Revealed_preference_rankings">Revealed preference rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=65" title="Edit section: Revealed preference rankings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Avery <i>et al.</i> pioneered the use of <a href="/wiki/Choice_modelling" title="Choice modelling">choice modelling</a> to rank colleges. Their methodology used a statistical analysis of the decisions of 3,240 students who applied to college in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> MyChances.net, now called Parchment, adopted a similar approach starting in 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> stating that its method is based on this approach.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> The study analysed students admitted to multiple colleges. The college they attended became the winner, and the others became the losers. An <a href="/wiki/Elo_rating_system" title="Elo rating system">Elo rating system</a> was used to assign points based on each win or loss, and the colleges were ranked based on their Elo points. A useful consequence of the use of Elo points is that they can be used to estimate the frequency with which students, upon being admitted to two schools, will choose one over the other. Most recent preference ranking placed Stanford at the top, followed by MIT, Harvard, and Princeton.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span id="Social_Mobility_Index_(SMI)_rankings"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_Mobility_Index_.28SMI.29_rankings">Social Mobility Index (SMI) rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=66" title="Edit section: Social Mobility Index (SMI) rankings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The SMI rankings are a collaborative publication from CollegeNet and PayScale. The rankings aim to provide a measure of the extent to which colleges provide upward economic mobility to those that attend. The rankings were created in response to the finding in Science magazine which showed that among developed nations, the United States now provides the least economic opportunity and mobility for its citizens. The rankings were also created to combat the rising costs of tuition, much of which is attributed to the efforts of some colleges to increase their own fame and wealth in ways that increase their rank in media periodicals that put an emphasis on such measures. According to the SMI, the top five colleges are Montana Tech, Rowan University, Florida A&amp;M, Cal Poly Pomona, and Cal State Northridge.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span id="U.S._News_&amp;_World_Report_college_and_university_rankings"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="U.S._News_.26_World_Report_college_and_university_rankings"><i>U.S. News &amp; World Report</i> college and university rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=67" title="Edit section: U.S. News &amp; World Report college and university rankings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2007_US_News_Top_40_colleges.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/2007_US_News_Top_40_colleges.png/250px-2007_US_News_Top_40_colleges.png" width="250" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/2007_US_News_Top_40_colleges.png/375px-2007_US_News_Top_40_colleges.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/2007_US_News_Top_40_colleges.png/500px-2007_US_News_Top_40_colleges.png 2x" data-file-width="738" data-file-height="498" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2007_US_News_Top_40_colleges.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Top 40 "National Universities" according to <i>U.S. News &amp; World Report</i>, 2007</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The magazine U.S. News &amp; World Report's college and university rankings have been compiled since 1983. The college rankings were published in all years thereafter, except 1984. The ranking order of universities has been shown to have great effect; a one-rank improvement leads to a 0.9% increase in number of applicants.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i>US News</i> rankings are based upon data which it collects from each educational institution either from an annual survey or from the school's website. There has been some significant controversy surrounding this annual survey, including a letter from the <a href="/wiki/Annapolis_Group" title="Annapolis Group">Annapolis Group</a> requesting that school presidents do not participate in the US News annual survey, which led to "a majority of the approximately 80 presidents at the meeting said that they did not intend to participate in the U.S. News reputational rankings in the future."<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> There have been reports of universities misreporting data on surveys just to gain an upper hand in rankings. <sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup></p>
<p>Also considered in the rankings formula are opinion surveys of university faculty and administrators outside the school.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup></p>
<p>U.S. News &amp; World Report puts the colleges in four separate categories based on whether they offer master's degrees, doctoral degrees, or only bachelor's degrees, and the extent to which these respective degree types are offered. In their Regional Colleges category their top colleges are: US Coast Guard Academy (North), Ashbury University (South), Taylor University (Midwest), and Carroll College (West). In their Regional Universities category their top colleges are: Villanova University (North), Elon (South), Creighton (Midwest), and Trinity University (West). In their Liberal Arts Colleges category their top colleges are: Williams, Amherst, Swarthmore, and Wellesley. Bowdoin and Pomona tie for fifth. In their National Universities category their top colleges are: Princeton, Harvard, the University of Chicago, Yale (tied for third), Columbia and Stanford (tied for fifth).<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_National_Research_Council_Rankings">United States National Research Council Rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=68" title="Edit section: United States National Research Council Rankings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Research_Council_Rankings" class="mw-redirect" title="United States National Research Council Rankings">United States National Research Council Rankings</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Research_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="United States National Research Council">National Research Council</a> ranks the doctoral research programmes of US universities, most recently in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> Data collection for an updated ranking began in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Faculty_Scholarly_Productivity_rankings">Faculty Scholarly Productivity rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=69" title="Edit section: Faculty Scholarly Productivity rankings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Faculty_Scholarly_Productivity_Index" title="Faculty Scholarly Productivity Index">Faculty Scholarly Productivity Index</a> by Academic Analytics ranks 354 institutions based on faculty publications, citations, research grants and awards.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Top_American_Research_Universities">The Top American Research Universities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=70" title="Edit section: The Top American Research Universities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p><a href="/wiki/Center_for_Measuring_University_Performance" title="Center for Measuring University Performance">The Center for Measuring University Performance</a> has ranked American research universities in the Top American Research Universities since 2000. The methodology is based on data such as research publications, citations, recognitions and funding, as well as undergraduate quality such as SAT scores. The information used can be found in publicly accessible materials, reducing possibilities for manipulation. The methodology is generally consistent from year to year and changes are explained in the publication along with references from other studies.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Washington_Monthly_College_rankings">Washington Monthly College rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=71" title="Edit section: Washington Monthly College rankings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Washington_Monthly" title="Washington Monthly">Washington Monthly</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s "College Rankings", last published in 2011, began as a research report in 2005. Related rankings appeared in the September 2006 issue. It offers American university and college rankings<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> based upon how well each enhances social mobility, fosters scientific and humanistic research and promotes an ethic of service.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> Washington Monthly puts the colleges in four separate categories based on whether they offer master's degrees, doctoral degrees, or only bachelor's degrees, and the extent to which these respective degree types are offered. In their Baccalaureate College category their top five are: Elizabeth City State University, Tuskegee University, Bethel College-North Newton, Wheeling Jesuit University, and Messiah College. In their Liberal Arts Colleges category their top five are: Bryn Mawr, Carleton College, Berea College, Swarthmore College, and Harvey Mudd. In their Master's Universities category their top five are: Creighton, Truman State, Valparaiso, Trinity University, and SUNY Geneseo. In their National Universities category their top five are: UC San Diego, UC Riverside, UC Berkeley, Texas A&amp;M, and UCLA.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="TrendTopper_MediaBuzz_College_Guide">TrendTopper MediaBuzz College Guide</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=72" title="Edit section: TrendTopper MediaBuzz College Guide">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p><a href="/wiki/TrendTopper_MediaBuzz_College_Guide" title="TrendTopper MediaBuzz College Guide">TrendTopper MediaBuzz College Guide</a> is an American-college guide based on what it calls "Internet brand equity" based on data collected from the Internet and global media sources. It ranks the Top 300 United States colleges and universities. The guide includes specialty and for profit schools including Art, Business, Design, Music, and Online Education. The TrendTopper MediaBuzz College Rankings are produced twice a year by the <a href="/wiki/Global_Language_Monitor" title="Global Language Monitor">Global Language Monitor</a> of <a href="/wiki/Austin" class="mw-redirect" title="Austin">Austin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Time_Magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="Time Magazine">Time Magazine</a> described internet brand equity as "a measure of who's talking about you online, based on Internet data, social media, blogs and the top 75,000 print and electronic media outlets."<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup></p>
<p>GLM ranks the schools "according to their online presence -- or internet brand equity ... By focusing on online presence, the Monitor hopes to avoid the biases that characterize other rankings, which commonly rely on the opinions of university officials and college counselors rather than that of the greater public.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> " GLM believes the rankings provide an up-to-date perspective on which schools have the most popular brand. The resulting rankings gauge the relative value of the various institutions and how they change over time.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="American_Council_of_Trustees_and_Alumni">American Council of Trustees and Alumni</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=73" title="Edit section: American Council of Trustees and Alumni">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>In 2009, the <a href="/wiki/American_Council_of_Trustees_and_Alumni" title="American Council of Trustees and Alumni">American Council of Trustees and Alumni</a> (ACTA) began grading each college or university on the strength of its general education requirements. ACTA's annual report on <i><a href="/wiki/What_Will_They_Learn%3F" title="What Will They Learn?">What Will They Learn?</a></i> uses how many of seven subjects (composition, mathematics, foreign language, science, economics, literature and American government or history) are required by an institution to assign it a letter grade (A through F).<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> The 2011-2012 edition of <i><a href="/wiki/What_Will_They_Learn%3F" title="What Will They Learn?">What Will They Learn?</a></i> graded 1,007 institutions,<sup id="cite_ref-aquinas_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aquinas-192">[192]</a></sup> and awarded nineteen schools an "A" for requiring more than five of the subjects.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> Its 2012-2013 evaluation awarded twenty one "A" grades among 1,070 colleges and universities.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup> ACTA's rating system has been endorsed by Mel Elfin, founding editor of U.S. News &amp; World Report's rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_Times" class="mw-redirect" title="New York Times">New York Times</a></i> higher education blogger <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Fish" title="Stanley Fish">Stanley Fish</a> agreed a university ought to have a strong core curriculum, but disagreed with the inclusion of some ACTA subjects in that core.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Niche_College_Rankings">Niche College Rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=74" title="Edit section: Niche College Rankings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Niche College Rankings is an American college ranking site that incorporates analysis of college based statistics and reviews. Niche also features A-F rankings for K-12 schools and neighborhoods or districts.<sup id="cite_ref-colleges.niche.com_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-colleges.niche.com-198">[198]</a></sup> Niche's rankings are updated every year. This is shown as they first developed college rankings by major as well as rankings and graded Report Cards for community colleges and trade schools.<sup id="cite_ref-colleges.niche.com_198-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-colleges.niche.com-198">[198]</a></sup> Niche provides its own grading system that applies a Bayesian method.<sup id="cite_ref-colleges.niche.com_198-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-colleges.niche.com-198">[198]</a></sup> In 2017, Niche provides several rankings in each category, "Best Colleges," "Best by Major," "Best by State," "Admissions," "Campus Life," "Student," and "Academics".<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> Niche collects more than 100 million college reviews and survey responses as well as comprehensive data such as U.S Department of Education.<sup id="cite_ref-colleges.niche.com_198-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-colleges.niche.com-198">[198]</a></sup> Niche also incorporates data from the new <i>College Scorecard Data</i> that was introduced in 2015 by the Obama Administration under the U.S Department of Education.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Other">Other</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=75" title="Edit section: Other">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Other organizations that rank US institutions include the <i>Fiske Guide to Colleges</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/College_Prowler" class="mw-redirect" title="College Prowler">College Prowler</a></i>. <i>Fiske Guide to Colleges</i> provides rankings for each criterion, which lets students choose their individual factors and use their rankings accordingly. Many specialized rankings are available in guidebooks, considering individual student interests, fields of study, geographical location, <a href="/wiki/Student_financial_aid_(United_States)" title="Student financial aid (United States)">financial aid</a> and affordability.</p>
<p>Among the rankings dealing with individual fields of study is the <a href="/wiki/Philosophical_Gourmet_Report" title="Philosophical Gourmet Report">Philosophical Gourmet Report</a> or "Leiter Report",<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> a ranking of <a href="/wiki/Philosophy" title="Philosophy">philosophy</a> departments. The PGR was described by <a href="/wiki/David_L._Kirp" title="David L. Kirp">David L. Kirp</a> in a 2003 <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">New York Times</a></i> op-ed as "the bible for prospective [philosophy] graduate students."<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> George Yancy, in <i>Reframing the Practice of Philosophy: Bodies of Color, Bodies of Knowledge</i> (<a href="/wiki/SUNY_Press" title="SUNY Press">SUNY Press</a>, 2012), opined that Philosophical Gourmet Report ranking: "is, of course, very controversial. However, as is often pointed out, there is no real alternative."<sup id="cite_ref-reframe_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reframe-202">[202]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Carlin_Romano" title="Carlin Romano">Carlin Romano</a>, in <i>America the Philosophical</i> (<a href="/wiki/Knopf_Doubleday_Publishing_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Knopf Doubleday Publishing Group">Knopf Doubleday Publishing Group</a>, 2013), referred to the PGR rankings as "often-criticized" and "biased towards mainstream analytic departments".<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> This report has attracted criticism from different viewpoints. Notably, practitioners of <a href="/wiki/Continental_philosophy" title="Continental philosophy">continental philosophy</a>, who perceive the Leiter report as unfair to their field, have compiled alternative rankings.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Gourman_Report" title="Gourman Report">Gourman Report</a>, last published in 1996, ranked the quality of undergraduate majors and graduate programs.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Gallup_poll" class="mw-redirect" title="Gallup poll">Gallup polls</a> ask American adults, "All in all, what would you say is the best college or university in the United States?"<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Guide to Online Schools</i> publishes online college rankings each year, using the criteria of recommendation rate, cost of tuition, retention rate, repayment rate, and accreditation. All schools on their 2013 online college rankings are regionally accredited.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Princeton_Review" class="mw-redirect" title="Princeton Review">Princeton Review</a>, annually publishes a book of Best Colleges. In 2011, this was titled <i>The Best 373 Colleges.</i> <a href="/wiki/Phi_Beta_Kappa" class="mw-redirect" title="Phi Beta Kappa">Phi Beta Kappa</a> has also sought to establish chapters at the best schools, lately numbering 280.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup></p>
<p>In terms of collegiate sports programs, the annual <a href="/wiki/NACDA_Directors%27_Cup" title="NACDA Directors' Cup">NACDA Directors' Cup</a> provides a measure of all-around collegiate athletic team achievement. Stanford has won the Division I Directors' cup for nineteen years in a row, and is poised to clinch its twentieth cup when the 2014 season ends.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup></p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Law_school_rankings_in_the_United_States" title="Law school rankings in the United States">Law school rankings in the United States</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oceania">Oceania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=76" title="Edit section: Oceania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Australia">Australia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=77" title="Edit section: Australia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Good_Universities_Guide&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="The Good Universities Guide (page does not exist)">The Good Universities Guide</a> and <a href="/wiki/Excellence_in_Research_for_Australia" title="Excellence in Research for Australia">Excellence in Research for Australia</a> annually rank domestic universities.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_America">South America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=78" title="Edit section: South America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="QS_University_Rankings:_Latin_America">QS University Rankings: Latin America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=79" title="Edit section: QS University Rankings: Latin America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>QS Quacquarelli Symonds, in addition to their QS World University Rankings, publish an annual ranking of the top 300 universities in Latin America. The eighth instalment, released for the 2016/17 academic year, places the Universidade de São Paulo as the region's best university.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Argentina">Argentina</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=80" title="Edit section: Argentina">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In Argentina the National Commission for University Evaluation and Accreditation ranks higher education programs by evaluation and accreditation.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Brazil">Brazil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=81" title="Edit section: Brazil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rankings_of_universities_in_Brazil" title="Rankings of universities in Brazil">Rankings of universities in Brazil</a></div>
<p>The latest ranking, the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://ruf.folha.uol.com.br/rankings/rankingdeuniversidades/">Ranking Universitário Folha (RUF)</a> website (in Portuguese), was created by the newspaper <a href="/wiki/Folha_de_S.Paulo" title="Folha de S.Paulo">Folha de S.Paulo</a>. This ranking is based on the combination of four indicators: education quality, research quality, market assessment and an innovation indicator.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Chile">Chile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=82" title="Edit section: Chile">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In Chile the "Comisión Nacional de Acreditación" (National Commission of Accreditation of the Universities) manages evaluation and accreditation. It also ranks universities according to accreditation levels.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> Other commercial rankings are made by research magazines, including <i>Qué Pasa</i> and <i>América Economía</i>. <i>Qué Pasa's</i> ranking evaluates perception and quality following surveys of approximately 1,000 employers across the country.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> <i>América Economía'</i>s ranking considers quality of students, quality of teachers, rating of professors by student, research productivity, internationalization, integration with the community, student life quality and inclusion of students from lower social strata.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=83" title="Edit section: Criticism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Critics argue that rankings can divert universities’ attention away from teaching and <a href="/wiki/Social_responsibility" title="Social responsibility">social responsibility</a> towards the type of scientific research valued by indicators used for ranking exercises. There have also been concerns that by applying a limited set of criteria to world universities, and given the strong desire to feature in the top 200 universities, rankings actually encourage the homogenization of higher education institutions, making them less responsive and less relevant to their immediate contexts. The fact that rankings are also said to favour the advantage enjoyed by the 200 best-ranked institutions has important implications for equity.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-215">[215]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=College_and_university_rankings&amp;action=edit&amp;section=84" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
